Let me re-check.\n\n`coalesce_x(layout, trg_profile)`:\n```cpp\nif constexpr (is_tuple<IntTuple>::value) {\n    return transform_layout(layout, trg_profile, ...);\n} else {\n    return coalesce_x(layout);\n}\n```\n\nSo if `trg_profile` is not a tuple (scalar 0), it just calls `coalesce_x(layout)` (full coalesce). \n\nWait, but `coprofile` returns `repeat_like(as_arithmetic_tuple(sum(stride)), 0)`. If `sum(stride)` is a scalar, this is `0`. So `coprofile(rhs) = 0` (scalar) for a flat rhs. For a hierarchical rhs... `sum(stride)` still returns a scalar because `sum` folds everything. So `coprofile(rhs) = 0` always (scalar).\n\nHold on. Let me double check `sum` on a tuple. `sum(((a,b),c)) = apply(((a,b),c), [...]) = 0 + sum((a,b)) + sum(c) = 0 + (0 + sum(a) + sum(b)) + sum(c) = a + b + c`. Yes, scalar. So `sum(stride)` is always a scalar.\n\nSo `coprofile(rhs) = repeat_like(as_arithmetic_tuple(scalar), 0) = repeat_like(scalar, 0) = 0`.\n\nTherefore `coalesce_x(lhs, coprofile(rhs)) = coalesce_x(lhs, 0) = coalesce_x(lhs)` (the full coalesce).\n\nSo the composition uses `coalesce_x(lhs)` — the full coalesce that preserves the function outside the domain!\n\nSo I need `coalesce_x`, not `coalesce`. The provided `coalesce` is the simpler one. I'll need to implement `coalesce_x` inside the composition (or as a helper) to match CUTLASS exactly.\n\nWait, let me reconsider. Maybe the difference between `coalesce` and `coalesce_x` doesn't matter for the test cases. But to be safe and exact, I should implement `coalesce_x`.\n\nLet me understand `coalesce_x` vs `coalesce`:\n\n`coalesce`:\n```cpp\nreturn bw_coalesce<R-2>(flat_shape, flat_stride, get<R-1>(flat_shape), get<R-1>(flat_stride));\n```\n\n`coalesce_x`:\n```cpp\nif constexpr (get<R-1>(flat_shape) == 1) {\n    return bw_coalesce<R-2>(flat_shape, flat_stride, Int<2>{}, get<R-1>(flat_stride));\n} else {\n    return bw_coalesce<R-2>(flat_shape, flat_stride, get<R-1>(flat_shape), get<R-1>(flat_stride));\n}\n```\n\nThe only difference: if the LAST mode's shape is 1, `coalesce_x` seeds with `Int<2>` (shape 2, stride = last stride) instead of (shape 1, last stride). The `Int<2>` shape is a trick: in `bw_coalesce`, the `is_constant<1, NewShape>` branch checks if `NewShape == 1`. By seeding with `2` (≠ 1), the \"Replace our shape-1 with anything\" branch won't trigger for the initial. Wait, but the merge branch checks `get<I>(old_shape) * get<I>(old_stride) == get<0>(new_stride)`.\n\nHmm, let me think about the difference with the example `(_4,_1):(_1,_0)`:\n- flat: shape=(4,1), stride=(1,0). R=2.\n- `coalesce`: `bw_coalesce<0>((4,1),(1,0), 1, 0)`. \n  - I=0: `get<0>(old_shape) = 4` (not 1). `NewShape = 1` → \"Replace our shape-1\" branch: `bw_coalesce<-1>((4,1),(1,0), get<0>(old_shape)=4, get<0>(old_stride)=1)`. \n  - I=-1: NewShape=4 (not 1) → return `Layout(4, 1)`. So coalesce gives `4:1`.\n- `coalesce_x`: last shape is 1, so seed with `(2, 0)`: `bw_coalesce<0>((4,1),(1,0), 2, 0)`.\n  - I=0: `get<0>(old_shape)=4` (not 1). NewShape=2 (not 1). Merge check: `get<0>(old_shape) * get<0>(old_stride) == get<0>(new_stride)`? `4 * 1 = 4 == 0`? (The accumulated shape-1 gets replaced by current mode.)\n3. `get<I>(old_shape) * get<I>(old_stride) == get<0>(new_stride)` AND new_shape is static (compile-time): merge — `new_shape = replace_front(new_shape, get<I>(old_shape) * get<0>(new_shape))`, `new_stride = replace_front(new_stride, get<I>(old_stride))`. I.e., prepend the product.\n4. Since we're building from the back and prepending, the first element is the most-recently-prepended one... Actually no.
